**Iran**,[^3] officially the **Islamic Republic of Iran**,[^4] historically known as **Persia**,[^5] is a country in [West Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Asia "West Asia"). It borders [Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq "Iraq") to the west, [Turkey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkey "Turkey"), [Azerbaijan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azerbaijan "Azerbaijan"), and [Armenia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenia "Armenia") to the northwest, the [Caspian Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caspian_Sea "Caspian Sea") to the north, [Turkmenistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkmenistan "Turkmenistan") to the northeast, [Afghanistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghanistan "Afghanistan") to the east, [Pakistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistan "Pakistan") to the southeast, and the [Gulf of Oman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_of_Oman "Gulf of Oman") and the [Persian Gulf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_Gulf "Persian Gulf") to the south. With a population of over 92 million, Iran ranks 17th globally in both [geographic size](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area "List of countries and dependencies by area") and [population](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population "List of countries and dependencies by population"). It is divided into [five regions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regions_of_Iran "Regions of Iran") with [31 provinces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Provinces_of_Iran "Provinces of Iran"). [Tehran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tehran "Tehran") is the nation's [capital](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capitals_of_Iran "Capitals of Iran") and [largest city](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Iran_by_province "List of cities in Iran by province") and serves as its primary economic centre.

Home to one of the world's oldest continuous major civilizations, the territory of present-day Iran was first unified under the [Medes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medes "Medes") in the 7th century BC and reached its territorial height in the 6th century BC, when [Cyrus the Great](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyrus_the_Great "Cyrus the Great") founded the [Achaemenid Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire "Achaemenid Empire"). [Alexander the Great](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_the_Great "Alexander the Great") conquered the empire in the 4th century BC.[^24] An Iranian rebellion in the 3rd century BC established the [Parthian Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parthian_Empire "Parthian Empire"), which later liberated the country. In the 3rd century AD, the Parthians were succeeded by the [Sasanian Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sasanian_Empire "Sasanian Empire"), which oversaw a golden age in the [history of Iranian civilization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Iran "History of Iran"). Ancient Iran saw some of the earliest developments of writing, agriculture, urbanization, religion, and administration. Once a center for [Zoroastrianism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zoroastrianism "Zoroastrianism"), Iran underwent [Islamization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamization_of_Iran "Islamization of Iran") following the [7th century Muslim conquest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_Persia "Muslim conquest of Persia"). Innovations in [literature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_literature "Persian literature"), [philosophy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_philosophy "Iranian philosophy"), mathematics, [medicine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Iranian_medicine "Ancient Iranian medicine"), astronomy and [art](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_art "Persian art") were renewed during the [Islamic Golden Age](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age "Islamic Golden Age") and [Iranian Intermezzo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Intermezzo "Iranian Intermezzo"), a period during which [Iranian Muslim dynasties](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_monarchs_of_Iran#Iranian_Intermezzo_\(821%E2%80%931090\) "List of monarchs of Iran") ended Arab rule and revived the [Persian language](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_language "Persian language"). This era was followed by [Seljuk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seljuk_Empire "Seljuk Empire") and [Khwarazmian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khwarazmian_Empire "Khwarazmian Empire") rule, [Mongol conquests](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mongol_conquest_of_Persia_and_Mesopotamia "Mongol conquest of Persia and Mesopotamia") and the [Timurid Renaissance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timurid_Renaissance "Timurid Renaissance") from the 11th to 14th centuries.

In the 16th century, the native [Safavid dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Safavid_Iran "Safavid Iran") re-established a unified Iranian state with [Twelver Shia Islam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Twelver_Shi%27ism "Twelver Shi'ism") as the [official religion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_religion "State religion"), laying the framework for the modern state of Iran. During the [Afsharid Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afsharid_Iran "Afsharid Iran") in the 18th century, Iran was a leading world power, but it lost this status after the [Qajars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qajar_Iran "Qajar Iran") took power in the 1790s. The early 20th century saw the [Persian Constitutional Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_Constitutional_Revolution "Persian Constitutional Revolution") and the establishment of the [Pahlavi dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pahlavi_dynasty "Pahlavi dynasty") by [Reza Shah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reza_Shah "Reza Shah"), who ousted the last Qajar Shah in 1925. Following the [Anglo-Soviet invasion of Iran in 1941](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anglo-Soviet_invasion_of_Iran "Anglo-Soviet invasion of Iran"), his son [Mohammad Reza Pahlavi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammad_Reza_Pahlavi "Mohammad Reza Pahlavi") rose to power. Attempts by [Mohammad Mosaddegh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammad_Mosaddegh "Mohammad Mosaddegh") to [nationalize the oil industry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nationalization_of_the_Iranian_oil_industry "Nationalization of the Iranian oil industry") led to the [Anglo-American coup in 1953](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1953_Iranian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat "1953 Iranian coup d'état"). The [Iranian Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Revolution "Iranian Revolution") in 1979 overthrew the monarchy, and the Islamic Republic of Iran was established by [Ruhollah Khomeini](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ruhollah_Khomeini "Ruhollah Khomeini"), the country's first [supreme leader](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Leader_of_Iran "Supreme Leader of Iran"). In 1980, [Iraq invaded Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraqi_invasion_of_Iran "Iraqi invasion of Iran"), sparking the eight-year-long [Iran–Iraq War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Iraq_War "Iran–Iraq War"). Iran has since been involved in [proxy wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proxy_war "Proxy war") with [Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Israel_proxy_conflict "Iran–Israel proxy conflict") and [Saudi Arabia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_war "Iran–Saudi Arabia proxy war"); in 2025, Israeli strikes on Iran escalated tensions into the [Twelve-Day War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Twelve-Day_War "Twelve-Day War"). Following the war and amid a [growing economic crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_economic_crisis "Iranian economic crisis"), the [largest protests since 1979](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2025%E2%80%932026_Iranian_protests "2025–2026 Iranian protests") erupted in 2025.[^25] [^26] The [United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States "United States") and [Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel "Israel") launched a [war with Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Iran_war "2026 Iran war") in 2026, after they [assassinated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assassination_of_Ali_Khamenei "Assassination of Ali Khamenei") supreme leader [Ali Khamenei](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_Khamenei "Ali Khamenei"). His son, [Mojtaba Khamenei](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mojtaba_Khamenei "Mojtaba Khamenei"), was subsequently [elected](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Iranian_supreme_leader_election "2026 Iranian supreme leader election") as his successor.[^27] [^28] [^29] [^30]

Iran's government is a [theocratic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theocracy#Islamic_theocracies "Theocracy") [Islamic republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_republic "Islamic republic") governed by elected and unelected institutions, with ultimate authority vested in the supreme leader. While [it holds elections](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elections_in_Iran "Elections in Iran"), key offices, including the head of state and military, are not subject to public vote. The Iranian government is an [authoritarian regime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarianism "Authoritarianism") which has been widely criticized internationally due to [poor human rights record](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_rights_in_the_Islamic_Republic_of_Iran "Human rights in the Islamic Republic of Iran"), including restrictions on [freedom of assembly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_of_assembly "Freedom of assembly"), [expression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_of_expression_in_Iran "Freedom of expression in Iran"), and the [press](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Media_of_Iran "Media of Iran"), as well as its [treatment of women](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women%27s_rights_in_Iran "Women's rights in Iran"), [ethnic minorities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_minorities_in_Iran "Ethnic minorities in Iran"), and [political dissidents](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_prisoners_in_Iran "Political prisoners in Iran"). The [Iranian economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economy_of_Iran "Economy of Iran") is centrally planned with significant state ownership in key sectors. It is a [regional power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regional_power "Regional power"), due to its large reserves of [fossil fuels](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fossil_fuel "Fossil fuel"), [natural gas supply](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_gas_in_Iran "Natural gas in Iran") and [oil reserves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_proven_oil_reserves "List of countries by proven oil reserves"), its geopolitically significant location, and its role as the world's focal point of [Shia Islam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia_Islam "Shia Islam").[^31] Iran is a [threshold state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_latency "Nuclear latency") with [one of the most scrutinized nuclear programs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_program_of_Iran "Nuclear program of Iran").[^32] [^33] It is a founding member of the UN and [a member state of numerous international organisations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Iran "Foreign relations of Iran"). Iran has 29 [UNESCO World Heritage Sites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_Iran "List of World Heritage Sites in Iran") (the [10th-highest in the world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Heritage_Sites_by_country "World Heritage Sites by country")) and ranks 4th in [intangible cultural heritage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intangible_cultural_heritage "Intangible cultural heritage") or human treasures.

## Etymology

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Persia_with_part_of_the_Ottoman_Empire%2C_1872.jpg/250px-Persia_with_part_of_the_Ottoman_Empire%2C_1872.jpg)

A map of West Asia in 1872, with "Iran or Persia", ruled by the Qajar dynasty, shaded in pink.

Historically, Iran was commonly referred to as "Persia" in the [Western world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_world "Western world").[^34] Likewise, the modern-day [ethnonym](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnonym "Ethnonym") "Persian" was typically used as a [demonym](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demonym "Demonym") for all Iranian nationals, regardless of whether or not they were [ethnic Persians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persians "Persians"). This terminology prevailed until 1935, when, during an international gathering for [Nowruz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nowruz "Nowruz"), the [Shah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shah "Shah") of Iran, [Reza Shah Pahlavi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reza_Shah "Reza Shah") officially requested that foreign delegates begin using the endonym ["Iran"](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran_\(word\) "Iran (word)") in formal correspondence. Subsequently, "Iran" and "Iranian" were standardised as the terms referring to the country and its citizens, respectively.[^35]

In 1959, the last Iranian Shah, [Mohammad Reza Pahlavi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammad_Reza_Pahlavi "Mohammad Reza Pahlavi"), announced that it was appropriate to use both "Persia" and "Iran" in formal correspondence.[^35] Dana Pishdar (Zana Vahidzadeh) notes that the terminology shift from "Persia" to "Iran" in 1935 was more than a mere change in foreign naming conventions; it represented a reclamation of national identity rooted deeply in the [region's long history](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Iran "History of Iran").[^36]

A variety of scholars from the [Middle Ages](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Ages "Middle Ages"), such as the [Khwarazmian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khwarazm "Khwarazm") polymath [Al-Biruni](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Biruni "Al-Biruni"), also used terms like " [Xuniras](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xuniras "Xuniras") " ([Avestan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avestan_language "Avestan language"): *Xvaniraθa-*, transl. "self-made, not resting on anything else") to refer to Iran: "which is the center of the world, \[...\] and it is the one wherein we are, and the kings called it the [Iranian realm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_realm "Iranian realm")." [^37]

## History

### Prehistory

The earliest known presence of hominins in Iran dates to around 800,000 years ago, in the [Middle Paleolithic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Paleolithic "Middle Paleolithic").[^38] Many Middle Paleolithic sites have been discovered, mainly in the [Zagros Mountains](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zagros_Mountains "Zagros Mountains") in western Iran and some sites associated with [Neanderthals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neanderthal "Neanderthal").[^39] [^40] The [Zarzian culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zarzian_culture "Zarzian culture") is documented in Iran during the [Epipaleolithic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Epipaleolithic "Epipaleolithic") (25,000–11,500 years ago).[^41] Agriculture first appeared in Iran some 12,000 years ago alongside better-documented settlements in the [Fertile Crescent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fertile_Crescent "Fertile Crescent"). The [Chogha Golan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chogha_Golan "Chogha Golan") site featured early domestication of [emmer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emmer "Emmer") wheat.[^42] The contemporary site of [Ganj Dareh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ganj_Dareh "Ganj Dareh") also features the earliest known domestication of [goats](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Goat "Goat") around 10,000 years ago.[^43]

The ancient city of [Susa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Susa "Susa"), which would become the capital of [Elam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elam "Elam") and later a capital city of the [Achaemenid empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Achaemenid_empire "Achaemenid empire"), was first settled in 4400–4200 BC, adjacent to the modern site of [Shush, Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shush,_Iran "Shush, Iran").[^44]<sup><span title="Page / location: 46–47">: 46–47</span> </sup> [^45] The [Kura–Araxes culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kura%E2%80%93Araxes_culture "Kura–Araxes culture") (c. 3400 – c. 2000 BC) existed in northwestern Iran and the [Caucasus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caucasus "Caucasus").[^46]

### Antiquity

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Choqa_Zanbil_Darafsh_1_%2836%29.JPG/250px-Choqa_Zanbil_Darafsh_1_%2836%29.JPG)

Chogha Zanbil is one of the few extant ziggurats outside of Mesopotamia and considered the best-preserved example in the world.

Iran is home to one of the world's oldest continuous major civilizations, with historical and urban settlements dating back to 4000 BC, including the [Jiroft culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jiroft_culture "Jiroft culture") in southeastern Iran.[^47] Inscriptions in the [Proto-Elamite script](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Elamite_script "Proto-Elamite script"), which predates [cuneiform](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuneiform "Cuneiform"), have been found from the early third millennium BC.[^48] [^49] The western part of the Iranian plateau participated in the traditional [ancient Near East](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Near_East "Ancient Near East") with [Elam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elam "Elam") (3200–539 BC), and later with other peoples such as the [Kassites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kassites "Kassites"), [Mannaeans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mannaea "Mannaea"), and [Gutians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gutians "Gutians"). The earliest Iranian peoples began to arrive from Central Asia in the 2nd millennium BC.[^50]

The [Median dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Median_dynasty#Genealogy "Median dynasty") ruled the earliest Iranian state.[^51] [^52] [^53] In 612 BC, [Cyaxares](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyaxares "Cyaxares") and the [Babylonian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Babylonia "Babylonia") king [Nabopolassar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nabopolassar "Nabopolassar") invaded [Assyria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assyria "Assyria") and destroyed [Nineveh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nineveh "Nineveh"), the Assyrian capital, which led to the fall of the [Neo-Assyrian Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neo-Assyrian_Empire "Neo-Assyrian Empire").[^54] The Medes later conquered and dissolved [Urartu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urartu "Urartu") as well.[^55] [^56] [^57]

#### Achaemenid Empire

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Achaemenid_Empire_at_its_greatest_extent_according_to_Oxford_Atlas_of_World_History_2002.jpg/330px-Achaemenid_Empire_at_its_greatest_extent_according_to_Oxford_Atlas_of_World_History_2002.jpg)

The Achaemenid Empire, or the First Persian Empire, at its greatest extent

The [Achaemenids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Achaemenid_dynasty "Achaemenid dynasty") united all [Persian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persians "Persians") tribes under [Cambyses I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cambyses_I "Cambyses I"). Under his son, [Cyrus the Great](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyrus_the_Great "Cyrus the Great"), the Achaemenids defeated the Medes and established the [Achaemenid Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire "Achaemenid Empire"),[^58] the largest-ever Iranian state.[^57] Cyrus conquered the [Lydian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lydia "Lydia") and [Neo-Babylonian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neo-Babylonian_Empire "Neo-Babylonian Empire") empires, creating an empire far larger than Assyria. His son, [Cambyses II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cambyses_II "Cambyses II") (r. 530–522 BC), conquered the last major power of the region, [ancient Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Egypt "Ancient Egypt"), causing the collapse of its [twenty-sixth dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Twenty-sixth_Dynasty_of_Egypt "Twenty-sixth Dynasty of Egypt").

After the death of Cambyses II, [Darius the Great](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Darius_the_Great "Darius the Great") (r. 522–486 BC) ascended the throne by overthrowing the Achaemenid monarch [Bardiya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bardiya "Bardiya"). Darius' first capital was at Susa, and he started the building program at [Persepolis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persepolis "Persepolis"). He improved the extensive road system, and during his reign the first recorded mentions are made of the [Royal Road](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Road "Royal Road"), a highway from Susa to [Sardis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sardis "Sardis").[^59]

In 499 BC, [Athens](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Classical_Athens "Classical Athens") supported a revolt in [Miletus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miletus "Miletus"), resulting in the sacking of Sardis. This led to the [Greco-Persian Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greco-Persian_Wars "Greco-Persian Wars"), which lasted the first half of the 5th century BC. In the [First Persian invasion of Greece](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Persian_invasion_of_Greece "First Persian invasion of Greece"), Persian general [Mardonius](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mardonius_\(general\) "Mardonius (general)") re-subjugated Thrace and made Macedon a full part of Persia.[^60] Darius' successor [Xerxes I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xerxes_I "Xerxes I") (r. 486–465) launched the [Second Persian invasion of Greece](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Persian_invasion_of_Greece "Second Persian invasion of Greece"). At a crucial moment in the war, about half of mainland Greece was overrun by the Persians, including territories to the north of the Isthmus of [Corinth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Corinth "Ancient Corinth").[^61] [^62] This was reversed by a Greek victory following the battles of [Plataea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Plataea "Battle of Plataea") and [Salamis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Salamis "Battle of Salamis"), during which Persia lost all of its footholds in Europe, and withdrew from it.[^63]

The empire entered a period of decline. From 334 BC to 331 BC, [Alexander the Great](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_the_Great "Alexander the Great") defeated [Darius III](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Darius_III "Darius III") (r. 336–330 BC) in the battles of [Granicus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_the_Granicus "Battle of the Granicus"), [Issus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Issus "Battle of Issus") and [Gaugamela](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Gaugamela "Battle of Gaugamela"), swiftly conquering the Achaemanid Empire by 331 BC. Alexander's empire collapsed after his death; his general, [Seleucus I Nicator](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seleucus_I_Nicator "Seleucus I Nicator"), tried to take control of Iran, [Mesopotamia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mesopotamia "Mesopotamia"), [Syria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syria "Syria"), and [Anatolia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anatolia "Anatolia"). His empire was the [Seleucid Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seleucid_Empire "Seleucid Empire").

#### Parthian and Sasanian empires

The Arsacids of [Parthia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parthia "Parthia"),[^64] initially Seleucid vassals,[^65] originated as leaders of the Iranian [^6] [Parni](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parni "Parni") tribe in the northeastern [steppes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steppe "Steppe").[^68] The Parthians gradually [challenged Seleucid rule](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seleucid%E2%80%93Parthian_Wars "Seleucid–Parthian Wars") over Iran, eventually securing control through the 142 BC conquest of [Babylonia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Babylonia "Babylonia").[^64] [^69] Although fighting continued, the death of [Antiochus VII Sidetes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antiochus_VII_Sidetes "Antiochus VII Sidetes") in 129 BC marked the collapse of the Seleucid Empire,[^69] which then lingered on as a [rump state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rump_state "Rump state") in Syria until conquered by the [Roman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Empire "Roman Empire") in the 60s BC.[^64]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/The_Sasanian_Empire_at_its_apex_under_Khosrow_II.svg/330px-The_Sasanian_Empire_at_its_apex_under_Khosrow_II.svg.png)

The Sasanian Empire at its greatest extent c. 620, under the reign of Khosrow II

The [Parthian Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parthian_Empire "Parthian Empire") endured for five centuries, but civil wars destabilized it. Parthian power evaporated when [Ardashir I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ardashir_I "Ardashir I") revolted against the Arsacids and killed their last ruler, [Artabanus IV](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artabanus_IV_of_Parthia "Artabanus IV of Parthia"), in 224 AD. Ardashir established the [Sasanian Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sasanian_Empire "Sasanian Empire"), which ruled Iran and much of [Near East](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Near_East "Near East").[^70] At their zenith, the Sasanians controlled all of modern-day Iran and Iraq and parts of the [Arabian Peninsula](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pre-Islamic_Arabia "Pre-Islamic Arabia"), as well as the [Caucasus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caucasus "Caucasus"), the [Levant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Levant "Levant"), and parts of [Central](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Asia "Central Asia") and [South Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Asia "South Asia").[^71]

The strong economic conditions left by Parthians allowed the Sasanians to build a powerful and distinctive economic state whose reputation spread well beyond its political frontiers and time.[^72] The Sasanian Empire was characterized by a complex and centralized government bureaucracy and the revitalization of [Zoroastrianism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zoroastrianism "Zoroastrianism") as a legitimizing and unifying ideal.[^73]

### Medieval period

Most of the Sasanian Empire's lifespan was overshadowed by the frequent [Byzantine–Sasanian wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine%E2%80%93Sasanian_wars "Byzantine–Sasanian wars"), a continuation of the [Roman–Parthian Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman%E2%80%93Parthian_Wars "Roman–Parthian Wars"). The last of these wars ultimately contributed to the [empire's fall](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fall_of_the_Sasanian_Empire "Fall of the Sasanian Empire"), which culminated with the [Islamic conquest of Persia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_Persia "Muslim conquest of Persia"). The [Rashidun Caliphate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rashidun_Caliphate "Rashidun Caliphate") conquered the Sasanian Empire between 632 and 654.

Over time, the majority of Iranians converted to [Islam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam "Islam"). Most of the aspects of the previous Persian civilizations were not discarded, but rather absorbed by the new Islamic polity.[^74]

#### Early Islamic rule and regional resistance in Iran

After the fall of the Sasanian Empire in 651, the [Arabs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs "Arabs") of the [Umayyad Caliphate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate "Umayyad Caliphate") adopted many Persian customs, especially the administrative and the court mannerisms. Arab provincial governors were undoubtedly either Persianized [Arameans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arameans "Arameans") or ethnic Persians; certainly, [Middle Persian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Persian_language "Middle Persian language") remained the language of official business of the caliphate until the adoption of Arabic toward the end of the seventh century.[^75]

However, Iran was still not entirely under Arab control; the [Daylam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daylam "Daylam") region was under the control of the [Daylamites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daylamites "Daylamites"), [Tabaristan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tabaristan "Tabaristan") was under [Dabuyid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dabuyid_dynasty "Dabuyid dynasty") and [Paduspanid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paduspanids "Paduspanids") control, and [Mount Damavand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mount_Damavand "Mount Damavand") under [Masmughan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Masmughans_of_Damavand "Masmughans of Damavand") control. Arabs had invaded these regions several times but the regions' inaccessible terrain prevented a decisive result. The most prominent ruler of the Dabuyids, [Farrukhan the Great](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Farrukhan_the_Great "Farrukhan the Great") (r. 712–728), managed to hold his domains during his long struggle against the Arab general [Yazid ibn al-Muhallab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yazid_ibn_al-Muhallab "Yazid ibn al-Muhallab"), who was defeated by a combined Daylamite–Dabuyid army and forced to retreat from Tabaristan.[^76]

#### The Abbasid revolution and Iranian Renaissance

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Saffarids_900ad.jpg/330px-Saffarids_900ad.jpg)

The Saffarid dynasty in 900 AD

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Iran_in_10th_century_AD.png/330px-Iran_in_10th_century_AD.png)

A map of Iranian dynasties in the mid 10th-century

Anti-Umayyad insurrections were supported by non-Arab Islamic converts, who were resentful over being relegated to lower social standing. In 747–750, one of these insurrections grew into the [Abbasid revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abbasid_revolution "Abbasid revolution"), in which the Umayyads were replaced with the [Abbasids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abbasid_dynasty "Abbasid dynasty"), descendants of Muhammad's uncle, [Abbas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abbas_ibn_Abd_al-Muttalib "Abbas ibn Abd al-Muttalib").[^77]

The political authority of the [Abbasid caliphs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate "Abbasid Caliphate") diminished over the course of the 9th and 10th centuries.[^78] This led to the establishment of several independent Iranian dynasties,[^78] the ousting of Arab rulers from their scattered bastions across the country, and an Iranian cultural renaissance.[^79] The period between the collapse of Abbasid authority and the conquest of Iran by the [Seljuk Turks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seljuk_Empire "Seljuk Empire") in the 11th century is referred to as the " [Iranian Intermezzo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Intermezzo "Iranian Intermezzo") ".[^79]

The Iranian Intermezzo saw the rise and fall of several major and minor dynasties.[^79] Among the most significant of these overlapping dynasties were the [Tahirids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tahirid_dynasty "Tahirid dynasty") in [Khorasan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greater_Khorasan "Greater Khorasan") (821–873); the [Saffarids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saffarid_dynasty "Saffarid dynasty") in [Sistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sistan "Sistan") (861–1003); and the [Samanids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samanid_Empire "Samanid Empire") (819–1005), originally at [Bukhara](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bukhara "Bukhara"). The Samanids eventually ruled an area from central Iran to Pakistan.

By the early 10th century, the Abbasids almost lost control to the growing Iranian faction known as the [Buyid dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buyid_dynasty "Buyid dynasty") (934–1062).[^80] Since much of the Abbasid administration had been Persian, the Buyids were quietly able to assume real power in Baghdad. The Buyids were defeated in the mid-11th century by the [Seljuq Turks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seljuk_Empire "Seljuk Empire"), who continued to exert influence over the Abbasids.

#### Islamization and Persianization

The [Islamization of Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamization_of_Iran "Islamization of Iran") was a long process. As Persian Muslims consolidated their rule, the Muslim population rose from approximately 40% in the mid-9th century to close to 90% by the end of the 11th century. Historian [Seyyed Hossein Nasr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seyyed_Hossein_Nasr "Seyyed Hossein Nasr") suggests that the rapid increase in conversion was aided by the Persian nationality of the rulers.[^81] Although Persians adopted the religion of their conquerors, over the centuries they worked to protect and revive their distinctive language and culture, a process known as [Persianization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persianization "Persianization"). Arabs and Turks participated in this process.[^82] [^83] [^84]

#### Mongol invasions

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Map_of_the_Khwarazmian_Empire.png/330px-Map_of_the_Khwarazmian_Empire.png)

Territory of the Khwarazmian Empire on the eve of the Mongol conquests, c. 1215

In the early 13th century, the Mongols reached Iran.[^85] [Bukhara was conquered](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Bukhara "Siege of Bukhara") in 1220 [^86] and the [Khwarazmian Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khwarazmian_Empire "Khwarazmian Empire") was destroyed.[^87] During 1220–21 Bukhara, [Samarkand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Samarkand_\(1220\) "Siege of Samarkand (1220)"), [Herat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herat "Herat"), [Tus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tus,_Iran "Tus, Iran") and [Nishapur](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nishapur "Nishapur") were razed, and the whole populations were slaughtered. Over the following decades, further conquests followed, culminating in the [fall of Baghdad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Baghdad "Siege of Baghdad") and end of the [Abbasid Caliphate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate "Abbasid Caliphate") 's rule in 1258.[^88]

After the death of [Möngke Khan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/M%C3%B6ngke_Khan "Möngke Khan"), the [Mongol Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mongol_Empire "Mongol Empire") was fractured by civil war, both over the succession of the next Great Khan and between nomadic traditionalists and the new settled princes of China and the Middle East. [Kublai Khan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kublai_Khan "Kublai Khan") was eventually universally recognized, but the empire was irreversibly fragmented.[^88] In much of the southwest of the empire, including Iran, power fell to [Hulegu Khan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hulegu_Khan "Hulegu Khan"),[^89] who had been made a deputy there under Möngke Khan.[^88] Hulegu was accepted as a legitimate ruler in Iran and was legitimized through a *[fatwa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fatwa "Fatwa")* issued by the Shia scholar [Ali ibn Tawus al-Hilli](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_ibn_Tawus_al-Hilli "Ali ibn Tawus al-Hilli").[^90] Iran experienced a cultural renaissance under [Ilkhanid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ilkhanate "Ilkhanate") rule.[^90] [Ghazan Khan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghazan_Khan "Ghazan Khan") converted to Islam in the late 13th century, turning the state further away from the other Mongol realms.[^89]

After Ghazan's nephew [Abu Said](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abu_Sa%27id_Bahadur_Khan "Abu Sa'id Bahadur Khan") died in 1335, the Ilkhanate lapsed into civil war and was divided between several petty dynasties – most prominently the [Jalayirids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jalayirids "Jalayirids"), [Muzaffarids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muzaffarids_\(Iran\) "Muzaffarids (Iran)"), [Sarbadars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sarbadars "Sarbadars") and [Kartids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kartids "Kartids"). The mid-14th-century [Black Death](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Death "Black Death") killed about 30% of the country's population.[^91]

#### Timur and the rise of new powers

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Empire_of_Timur_and_his_Campaigns.png/250px-Empire_of_Timur_and_his_Campaigns.png)

Timur 's empire and his military campaigns

Iran remained divided until the establishment of the Persianate [Timurid dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timurid_dynasty "Timurid dynasty") in 1370. Its founder, Timur (r. 1370–1405), hailed from a [Turkified](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkification "Turkification") tribe of Mongols.[^92] After establishing a power base in [Transoxiana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transoxiana "Transoxiana"), Timur invaded Iran in 1381 and eventually conquered most of it. Timur's campaigns were known for their brutality; many people were slaughtered and several cities were destroyed.[^93]

In 1387, Timur ordered the complete [massacre of Isfahan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Isfahan_\(1387\) "Siege of Isfahan (1387)"), killing 70,000 people.[^94] The Timurids maintained control of most of Iran until 1452, when they lost the bulk of it to the [Qara Qoyunlu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qara_Qoyunlu "Qara Qoyunlu"), who were conquered by the [Aq Qoyunlu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aq_Qoyunlu "Aq Qoyunlu") in 1468. [Uzun Hasan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uzun_Hasan "Uzun Hasan") and his successors were the masters of Iran until the rise of the Safavids.[^93]

### Early modern period

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Safavid_Empire_1501_1722_AD.png/250px-Safavid_Empire_1501_1722_AD.png)

Safavid Iran (1501–1722) at its greatest extent

The [Safavid Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Safavid_Iran "Safavid Iran"), founded by [Ismail I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ismail_I "Ismail I") (r. 1505–1524), is often considered the beginning of modern Iranian history.[^95] While Safavid Iran predated the concept of the nation-state as such, it established the basis for the modern state of Iran.[^95] [^96] The [Safavid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Safavid_dynasty "Safavid dynasty") dynastic period was one of the most important in Iranian history, as it reunified Iran as a cohesive entity under native rule and established Shia Islam as the [official religion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_religion "State religion").[^97] The Safavids ruled from 1501 to 1722, and experienced a brief restoration from 1729 to 1736.

The Safavid state had a complex bureaucratic system of checks and balances, which ensured transparency and prevented fraud. This system was not intended to equalize power between branches of government, but to ensure total power of the shah. Legitimized by his bloodline as a [sayyid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sayyid "Sayyid"), or descendant of Muhammad, the shah monitored the actions of government officials through reports provided by the superintendent of each department. [Jean Chardin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean_Chardin "Jean Chardin"), French merchant and eventual ambassador to Iran, wrote that the Safavid shahs ruled their land with an iron fist and often in a [despotic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Despotism "Despotism") manner.[^98]

Complex rivalries in the region of [Khorasan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greater_Khorasan "Greater Khorasan") led to the Afghan [Hotak dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hotak_dynasty "Hotak dynasty") invading Iran. In 1722, this conflict led to the collapse of the Safavid Empire after the [siege of Isfahan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Isfahan "Siege of Isfahan").[^95] [^99] The brief interlude between 1722 and the rise of the [Qajar dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qajar_dynasty "Qajar dynasty") in 1789–1796 was marked by widespread political turmoil in Iran and several rival attempts to establish power over the country. The Safavids failed to regain power and the Hotaks failed to establish control. The rival [Afsharid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afsharid_Iran "Afsharid Iran") and [Zand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zand_dynasty "Zand dynasty") dynasties were established by [Nader Shah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nader_Shah "Nader Shah") (r. 1736–1747) and [Karim Khan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karim_Khan_Zand "Karim Khan Zand") (r. 1751–1779), respectively.[^99]

#### Nader Shah and the shifting balance of power

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Revised_Map_of_the_Afsharid_Empire.png/250px-Revised_Map_of_the_Afsharid_Empire.png)

A map of the Afsharid Empire at its greatest extent, in 1741–1745

Nader Shah has been described as "the last great Asiatic military conqueror", and compared by some historians to Napoleon and Alexander the Great.[^100] [^101] His numerous campaigns created a great empire that, at its maximum extent, briefly encompassed all or part of modern-day Afghanistan, Armenia, Azerbaijan, Bahrain, Georgia, India, Iran, Iraq, Turkey, Turkmenistan, Oman, Pakistan, Uzbekistan, the [North Caucasus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Caucasus "North Caucasus"), and the [Persian Gulf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_Gulf "Persian Gulf"). However, his military spending had a ruinous effect on the Iranian economy.[^102]

Nader Shah's death was followed by a [period of anarchy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Division_of_the_Afsharid_Empire "Division of the Afsharid Empire") in Iran as rival army commanders fought for power. Nader's own family, the [Afsharids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afsharid_dynasty "Afsharid dynasty"), lost all but a small domain in Khorasan. The Zand family seized control of much of Iran in the 1750s.[^103] The Zand rulers never proclaimed themselves to be *shah* s, but as [regents](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regent "Regent") of Iran.[^103] *[^104]* They first staked their claim to power on behalf of the Safavid puppet [Ismail III](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ismail_III "Ismail III") (r. 1750–1773) and then on behalf of the Iranian people.[^103] *[^104]*

#### Rise of the Qajar dynasty and foreign interference

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Map_Iran_1900-en.png/250px-Map_Iran_1900-en.png)

Iran under the Qajar dynasty in the 19th century.

The Qajar dynasty gradually increased in power as they clashed with the Afsharids and the Zands for control of the land, culminating in [Agha Mohammad Shah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agha_Mohammad_Shah "Agha Mohammad Shah") proclaiming himself ruler in 1789.[^105] Agha Mohammad defeated the Zand dynasty in 1794 and was officially crowned in 1796.[^103] [^105] Shortly thereafter, he captured and deposed the Afsharid Shahrokh Shah, reunifying Iran under a single ruler.[^105]

In the 19th century, Iran lost significant territories in the [Caucasus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caucasus "Caucasus") to the [Russian Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Empire "Russian Empire") following the [Russo-Persian Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo-Persian_Wars "Russo-Persian Wars").[^106] Meanwhile, [Britain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Kingdom "United Kingdom") became involved in [southern Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Iran "Southern Iran") to counter Russia's presence in the north, which posed a threat to [British India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_India "British India").[^107] Amid this struggle for power, drought, shifting agricultural priorities, and poor governance culminated in the [Great Persian Famine of 1870–1871](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_famine_of_1870%E2%80%931872 "Persian famine of 1870–1872"). While the death toll is unknown, the famine killed a significant portion of Iran's population; between several hundred thousand and four million Iranians are believed to have died as a result.[^108]

### 20th century up to the Iranian Revolution

#### Constitutional Revolution and the rise of the Pahlavi dynasty

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/RezaShahBozorgTakhteJamshid32.jpg/250px-RezaShahBozorgTakhteJamshid32.jpg)

Reza Shah with then-Crown Prince Mohammad Reza Pahlavi at Persepolis, c. 1939

The [Persian Constitutional Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_Constitutional_Revolution "Persian Constitutional Revolution") between 1905 and 1911 led to the establishment of an Iranian parliament.[^109] After the [1921 coup d'état](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1921_Persian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat "1921 Persian coup d'état"), the Qajar dynasty was replaced with the [Pahlavi dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pahlavi_dynasty "Pahlavi dynasty").[^110] The dynasty was founded by [Reza Shah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reza_Shah "Reza Shah"), who established an [authoritarian government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarianism "Authoritarianism") that valued [nationalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_nationalism "Iranian nationalism"), [militarism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Militarism "Militarism"), [secularism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secularism_in_Iran "Secularism in Iran") and [anti-communism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-communism "Anti-communism") combined with strict [censorship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Censorship "Censorship") and [state propaganda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_propaganda "State propaganda").[^111] Reza Shah introduced many socio-economic reforms, reorganizing the army, government administration, and finances.[^112] Reza Shah ruled for almost 16 years until 1941, when he was forced to [abdicate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdication "Abdication") by the [Anglo-Soviet invasion of Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anglo-Soviet_invasion_of_Iran "Anglo-Soviet invasion of Iran").

To his supporters, his reign brought " [law and order](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law_and_order_\(politics\) "Law and order (politics)"), discipline, central authority, and modern amenities – schools, trains, buses, radios, cinemas, and telephones." [^113] However, his reign has been characterized as a corrupt [police state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Police_state "Police state") which provided only surface level modernization.[^113] [^114] [^115]

#### World War II and post-occupation instability

Due in part to Nazi Germany's [invasion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa "Operation Barbarossa") of the [Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union"), the Iranian government expected Germany to win the war and establish a powerful force on the Russian-Iranian border. Iran rejected British and Soviet demands to expel German residents from its borders. In response, the two [Allies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II "Allies of World War II") invaded in August 1941 and easily overwhelmed the weak Iranian army in [Operation Countenance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Countenance "Operation Countenance").[^116]

Iran became the major conduit of Allied [Lend-Lease](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lend-Lease "Lend-Lease") aid to the Soviet Union. The purpose was to secure Iranian oil fields and ensure Allied supply lines through the [Persian Corridor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_Corridor "Persian Corridor"). Iran remained officially neutral. Reza Shah was deposed during the subsequent occupation and replaced with his young son [Mohammad Reza Pahlavi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammad_Reza_Pahlavi "Mohammad Reza Pahlavi").[^116] At the 1943 [Tehran Conference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tehran_Conference "Tehran Conference"), the Allied "Big Three"— [Joseph Stalin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Stalin "Joseph Stalin"), [Franklin D. Roosevelt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt "Franklin D. Roosevelt"), and [Winston Churchill](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winston_Churchill "Winston Churchill") —issued the Tehran Declaration to guarantee the post-war independence and boundaries of Iran.[^117]

#### Mosaddegh and the Shah's rule

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Pahlavi_family_coronation_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Pahlavi_family_coronation_%28cropped%29.jpg)

The coronation of Mohammad Reza Pahlavi, the last Iranian coronation, held in 1967

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Jimmy_Carter_with_King_Hussein_of_Jordan_the_Shah_of_Iran_and_Shahbanou_of_Iran_-_NARA_-_177332_04.jpg/250px-Jimmy_Carter_with_King_Hussein_of_Jordan_the_Shah_of_Iran_and_Shahbanou_of_Iran_-_NARA_-_177332_04.jpg)

Mohammad Reza Shah and Shahbanu Farah Pahlavi of Iran with US President Jimmy Carter and King Hussein of Jordan in 1977

In 1951, under Prime Minister [Mohammad Mosaddegh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammad_Mosaddegh "Mohammad Mosaddegh"), the Iranian parliament voted to nationalize the British-owned oil industry, leading to the [Abadan Crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abadan_Crisis "Abadan Crisis"). Despite British pressure, including an economic blockade, nationalization continued. Mosaddegh was removed from power in 1952 but was quickly re-appointed by the Shah, due to a popular uprising in support of the premier. He forced the Shah into a brief exile in August 1953 after a failed military coup by [Imperial Guard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperial_Guard_\(Iran\) "Imperial Guard (Iran)") Colonel [Nematollah Nassiri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nematollah_Nassiri "Nematollah Nassiri").

On 19 August, a successful [coup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1953_Iranian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat "1953 Iranian coup d'état") was headed by retired army general [Fazlollah Zahedi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fazlollah_Zahedi "Fazlollah Zahedi"), aided by the US ([CIA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CIA "CIA")) [^118] and the British ([MI6](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MI6 "MI6")), known as Operation Ajax and Operation Boot to the respective agencies.[^119] The coup—with a [black propaganda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_propaganda "Black propaganda") campaign against Mosaddegh [^120] —forced Mosaddegh from office. Mosaddegh was arrested and tried for treason. Found guilty, Mosaddegh had his sentence reduced to house arrest on his family estate while his foreign minister, [Hossein Fatemi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hossein_Fatemi "Hossein Fatemi"), was executed. Zahedi succeeded him as prime minister and suppressed opposition to the Shah, specifically from the [National Front](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Front_\(Iran\) "National Front (Iran)") and the communist [Tudeh Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tudeh_Party "Tudeh Party").

From that time until the revolution, Iran was ruled as an autocracy under the Shah, with strong American support. Iran initiated economic, social, agrarian, and administrative reforms to modernize the country, which became known as the [White Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_Revolution "White Revolution"). Many Islamic leaders criticized these initiatives, and the land reform had mixed results.[^121] By 1978, the Shah had become wildly unpopular among the Iranian people. Daily demonstrations destabilized the region, and the Shah established [martial law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martial_law "Martial law") to curb opposition. When hundreds of thousands of protestors persisted, security forces opened fire on the crowds in an incident that became known as [Black Friday](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Friday_\(1978\) "Black Friday (1978)").[^122]

### Islamic Revolution

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Imam_Khomeini_in_Mehrabad.jpg/250px-Imam_Khomeini_in_Mehrabad.jpg)

Ruhollah Khomeini returns to Iran after 14 years of exile in Turkey, Iraq and France on 1 February 1979.

The protests against the Shah grew to include more than 10% of the country; it is rare for revolutions to involve even 1% of a country's population.[^123] Frustration with the Shah was so great that even secular and leftist groups supported [Ayatollah Ruhollah Khomeini](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ruhollah_Khomeini "Ruhollah Khomeini"), the leader of the [revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Revolution "Iranian Revolution"), despite sharing none of his political positions.[^124] Under increasing pressure, the Shah eventually fled Iran, charging the interim [Regency Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regency_Council_\(Iran\) "Regency Council (Iran)") with his duties until a new government was formed.[^125] [^126] [Shapour Bakhtiar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shapour_Bakhtiar "Shapour Bakhtiar"), the head of the council, invited Khomeini to return from exile. However, upon return, Khomeini pledged to defeat the interim government led by Bakhtiar and claimed to support free democratic elections. Violence broke out between the two factions, ultimately leading Bakhtiar to flee Iran in disguise.

On 31 March 1979, a [referendum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1979_Iranian_Islamic_Republic_referendum "1979 Iranian Islamic Republic referendum") was held on whether to transition from a government of monarchy to an [Islamic republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_republic "Islamic republic"). The referendum was approved by a massive margin of 99.31%. It mandated the creation of an [assembly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assembly_for_the_Final_Review_of_the_Constitution "Assembly for the Final Review of the Constitution") to draft the new [theocratic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theocratic "Theocratic") constitution, whereby Khomeini became [Supreme Leader](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Leader_of_Iran "Supreme Leader of Iran") in December 1979. Iran's modernizing, capitalist economy was replaced by populist Islamic economic and cultural policies. Industries were nationalized, laws and schools [Islamized](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamization_of_knowledge "Islamization of knowledge"), and [Western influence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_world "Western world") restricted.[^127]

#### Khomeini era, Iran–Iraq War, and leadership transition

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Chemical_weapon1.jpg/250px-Chemical_weapon1.jpg)

An Iranian soldier with gas mask during the Iran–Iraq War

The shah, now out of power, went to the US to seek cancer treatment after other countries denied him entry. Supporters of the revolution feared that this was a step toward a coup to reinstate the Shah's reign. On 4 November 1979, Iranian students [seized US embassy personnel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran_hostage_crisis "Iran hostage crisis"), labeling the embassy a "den of spies".[^128] 52 hostages were held for 444 days until January 1981.[^129] During the [Cultural Revolution in Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cultural_Revolution_in_Iran "Cultural Revolution in Iran") from 1980 to 1983, opposition to Islamic values was purged [^130] including through the [1981–1982 Iran massacres](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1981%E2%80%931982_Iran_massacres "1981–1982 Iran massacres").[^131]

Iraqi leader [Saddam Hussein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saddam_Hussein "Saddam Hussein") attempted to take advantage of the disorder of the revolution, the weakness of the Iranian military and the revolution's antagonism against Western governments. On 22 September 1980, the Iraqi army [invaded Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraqi_invasion_of_Iran "Iraqi invasion of Iran") at [Khuzestan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khuzestan_province "Khuzestan province"), precipitating the [Iran–Iraq War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Iraq_War "Iran–Iraq War"). The attack took revolutionary Iran by surprise. Although Hussein's forces made early advances, Iranian forces pushed the Iraqi army back into Iraq by 1982.[^132]

Khomeini sought to [export the revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exporting_the_revolution "Exporting the revolution") westward into Iraq, especially to Iraq's Shi'a Arab majority. The war continued until 1988, when Khomeini "drank the cup of poison" and accepted a truce mediated by the UN.[^132] The war, which ended in a stalemate in 1988, killed approximately 500,000 people.[^133] During the war, Saddam extensively used [chemical weapons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraqi_chemical_weapons_program "Iraqi chemical weapons program") against Iranians.[^134]

#### Khamenei era

On his deathbed in 1989, Khomeini appointed a 25-man Constitutional Reform Council, which named [Ali Khamenei](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_Khamenei "Ali Khamenei") as the next Supreme Leader, and made changes to Iran's constitution.[^135] While Khamenei lacked Khomeini's "charisma and clerical standing", he developed a network of supporters within the armed forces and its economically powerful [religious foundations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bonyad "Bonyad").[^136]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Ayatollah_Ali_Khamenei_at_the_Great_Conference_of_Basij_members_at_Azadi_stadium_October_2018_033.jpg/250px-Ayatollah_Ali_Khamenei_at_the_Great_Conference_of_Basij_members_at_Azadi_stadium_October_2018_033.jpg)

Ali Khamenei at the Great Conference of Basij members at Azadi Stadium, October 2018

President [Akbar Rafsanjani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Akbar_Rafsanjani "Akbar Rafsanjani") concentrated on a pro-business policy of rebuilding the economy, without breaking with the ideology of the revolution. He supported a free market, favoring privatization of state industries and a moderate position internationally. In 1997, Rafsanjani was succeeded by moderate [reformist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_reform_movement "Iranian reform movement") [Mohammad Khatami](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammad_Khatami "Mohammad Khatami"), whose government advocated freedom of expression, constructive diplomatic relations with Asia and the EU, and policy that supported a free market and foreign investment.

The [2005 presidential election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2005_Iranian_presidential_election "2005 Iranian presidential election") brought conservative populist and nationalist candidate [Mahmoud Ahmadinejad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahmoud_Ahmadinejad "Mahmoud Ahmadinejad") to power. He was known for his hardline views, nuclearization, and [hostility towards Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahmoud_Ahmadinejad_and_Israel "Mahmoud Ahmadinejad and Israel"), [Saudi Arabia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabia "Saudi Arabia"), the UK, US and other states. He was the first president to be summoned by the [parliament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Consultative_Assembly "Islamic Consultative Assembly") to answer questions regarding his presidency.[^137] In 2013, centrist and reformist [Hassan Rouhani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hassan_Rouhani "Hassan Rouhani") was elected president. He encouraged personal freedom, access to information, and improved women's rights. He improved diplomatic relations through exchanging conciliatory letters.[^138]

In 2015, the [Joint Comprehensive Plan of Action](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joint_Comprehensive_Plan_of_Action "Joint Comprehensive Plan of Action") was reached in [Vienna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vienna "Vienna"), between Iran, the [P5+1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/P5%2B1 "P5+1") ([UN Security Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Permanent_members_of_the_United_Nations_Security_Council "Permanent members of the United Nations Security Council") + Germany) and the EU. The negotiations centered around ending the [economic sanctions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1929 "United Nations Security Council Resolution 1929") in exchange for Iran's restriction in producing [enriched uranium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enriched_uranium "Enriched uranium").[^139] In 2018, the US under President [Donald Trump](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_presidency_of_Donald_Trump "First presidency of Donald Trump") withdrew from the deal and new sanctions were imposed. This nulled the economic provisions and brought Iran to [nuclear threshold status](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_latency "Nuclear latency").[^140]

In 2020, [IRGC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Revolutionary_Guard_Corps "Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps") general [Qasem Soleimani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qasem_Soleimani "Qasem Soleimani"), the 2nd-most powerful person in Iran,[^141] was [assassinated by the US](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assassination_of_Qasem_Soleimani "Assassination of Qasem Soleimani"), heightening [tensions between them](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Iran–United States relations").[^142] [Iran retaliated against US airbases in Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Martyr_Soleimani "Operation Martyr Soleimani"), the largest ballistic missile attack ever on Americans;[^143] 110 sustained [brain injuries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Traumatic_brain_injury "Traumatic brain injury").[^144] [^145] [^146] On 8 January, Iran's Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps shot down [Ukraine International Airlines Flight 752](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukraine_International_Airlines_Flight_752 "Ukraine International Airlines Flight 752"), killing 176 civilians and leading to [nation-wide protests](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukraine_International_Airlines_Flight_752_protests "Ukraine International Airlines Flight 752 protests"). An international investigation led to the government admitting to the shootdown by a surface-to-air missile.[^147] [^148]

Hardliner [Ebrahim Raisi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ebrahim_Raisi "Ebrahim Raisi") lost a presidential bid in 2017, but ran again [in 2021](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021_Iranian_presidential_election "2021 Iranian presidential election"), succeeding Rouhani.[^149] During Raisi's term, Iran [intensified uranium enrichment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_program_of_Iran "Nuclear program of Iran"), hindered international inspections, joined SCO and BRICS, [supported the](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran_and_the_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine "Iran and the Russian invasion of Ukraine") [2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine "2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine") and restored relations with Saudi Arabia. In April 2024, an [Israeli airstrike on the Iranian consulate in Damascus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_airstrike_on_the_Iranian_consulate_in_Damascus "Israeli airstrike on the Iranian consulate in Damascus") killed an IRGC commander.[^150] [^151] Iran [retaliated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/April_2024_Iranian_strikes_on_Israel "April 2024 Iranian strikes on Israel") with [UAVs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unmanned_aerial_vehicle "Unmanned aerial vehicle"), [cruise](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cruise_missile "Cruise missile") and [ballistic missiles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ballistic_missile "Ballistic missile"); 9 hit Israel.[^152] [^153] [^154] It was the largest drone strike in history,[^155] biggest missile attack in Iranian history,[^156] its first ever direct attack on Israel [^157] [^158] and the first time [since 1991](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1991_Iraqi_missile_attacks_against_Israel "1991 Iraqi missile attacks against Israel") that Israel was directly attacked by a state.[^159]

In May 2024, Raisi was killed in [a helicopter crash](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_Varzaqan_helicopter_crash "2024 Varzaqan helicopter crash"),[^160] and Iran held a [presidential election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_Iranian_presidential_election "2024 Iranian presidential election"), when reformist and former [Minister of Health](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Health_and_Medical_Education "Ministry of Health and Medical Education"), [Masoud Pezeshkian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Masoud_Pezeshkian "Masoud Pezeshkian"), was elected.[^161] [^162] In October, Iran [launched](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/October_2024_Iranian_strikes_on_Israel "October 2024 Iranian strikes on Israel") 180 ballistic missiles at Israel in retaliation for assassinations [of Ismail Haniyeh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assassination_of_Ismail_Haniyeh "Assassination of Ismail Haniyeh"), [Hassan Nasrallah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_Hezbollah_headquarters_strike "2024 Hezbollah headquarters strike") and [Abbas Nilforoushan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abbas_Nilforoushan "Abbas Nilforoushan"). Israel [struck](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/October_2024_Israeli_strikes_on_Iran "October 2024 Israeli strikes on Iran") Iranian military sites.[^163] In May 2025, Iran's government ordered [a mass deportation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2025_Afghan_deportation_from_Iran "2025 Afghan deportation from Iran") of an estimated four million [Afghan migrants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghan_diaspora "Afghan diaspora") and refugees living in Iran.[^164]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/%D8%AA%D9%82%D8%AF%DB%8C%D9%85_%D9%BE%DB%8C%D8%A7%D9%85_%D9%BE%D8%A7%D8%AF%D8%B4%D8%A7%D9%87_%D8%B9%D8%B1%D8%A8%D8%B3%D8%AA%D8%A7%D9%86_%D8%A8%D9%87_%D8%B1%D9%87%D8%A8%D8%B1_%D8%A7%D9%86%D9%82%D9%84%D8%A7%D8%A8_07.jpg/250px-%D8%AA%D9%82%D8%AF%DB%8C%D9%85_%D9%BE%DB%8C%D8%A7%D9%85_%D9%BE%D8%A7%D8%AF%D8%B4%D8%A7%D9%87_%D8%B9%D8%B1%D8%A8%D8%B3%D8%AA%D8%A7%D9%86_%D8%A8%D9%87_%D8%B1%D9%87%D8%A8%D8%B1_%D8%A7%D9%86%D9%82%D9%84%D8%A7%D8%A8_07.jpg)

Ayatollah Ali Khamenei with Saudi Arabia 's Defense Minister Khalid bin Salman and Major General Mohammad Bagheri on 17 April 2025

The weakening of Iran's [key allies and proxies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Axis_of_Resistance "Axis of Resistance") since 2023 left Iran's government weakened and isolated.[^165] [^166] [^167] In early 2025, Iran was rapidly advancing its nuclear program.[^168] Analysts warned such activity exceeded any plausible civilian justification.[^169] Iran and the United States [entered negotiations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2025%E2%80%932026_Iran%E2%80%93United_States_negotiations "2025–2026 Iran–United States negotiations") for a new nuclear agreement, but progress stalled. In June, [IAEA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Atomic_Energy_Agency "International Atomic Energy Agency") found Iran non-compliant with its nuclear obligations;[^170] in response, Iran announced activation of a new enrichment facility.[^171]

On 13 June 2025, Israel launched strikes across Iran, targeting nuclear facilities and killing top members of Iran's military leadership.[^172] [^173] Iran retaliated with missile strikes, and hostilities resulted in [direct conflict](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Twelve-Day_War "Twelve-Day War") between them. On 22 June, the [US struck the Iranian nuclear facilities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_strikes_on_Iranian_nuclear_sites "United States strikes on Iranian nuclear sites").[^174] Iran [attacked US bases in Qatar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2025_Iranian_strikes_on_Al_Udeid_Air_Base "2025 Iranian strikes on Al Udeid Air Base") as a result. On 24 June, Israel and Iran agreed to a ceasefire after insistence from the US.[^175] [^176]

Since December 2025, Iran [has had mass demonstrations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2025%E2%80%932026_Iranian_protests "2025–2026 Iranian protests") across cities calling for the overthrow of the Islamic Republic, sparked by frustration over [the economic crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_economic_crisis "Iranian economic crisis").[^177] As of 13 January 2026, *[Iran International](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran_International "Iran International")* estimated that at least 12,000 protesters had been killed amidst the [internet blackout](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Internet_blackout_in_Iran "2026 Internet blackout in Iran"), as government security forces escalated their use of lethal force against demonstrators.[^178] [^179] [^180] As of 17 January 2026, estimates suggested that at least 16,500 people had been killed and approximately 330,000 injured in the [2026 Iran massacres](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Iran_massacres "2026 Iran massacres").[^181]

On 28 February 2026, the [United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States "United States") and [Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel "Israel") conducted [coordinated military strikes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Israeli%E2%80%93United_States_strikes_on_Iran "2026 Israeli–United States strikes on Iran") against multiple targets in the Islamic Republic of Iran, marking a significant escalation in long-standing tensions between [Tehran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tehran "Tehran") and the [U.S.–Israel alliance.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Israel–United States relations")[^182] That same day, Ali Khamenei [was assassinated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assassination_of_Ali_Khamenei "Assassination of Ali Khamenei") as part of a series of Israeli airstrikes [aimed at high-ranking Iranian officials](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Iranian_officials_killed_during_the_2026_Iran_war "List of Iranian officials killed during the 2026 Iran war"). Khamenei's death was confirmed by the Iranian government on 1 March.[^183] On 8 March, the 88-person Assembly of Experts announced that [Mojtaba Khamenei](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mojtaba_Khamenei "Mojtaba Khamenei"), son of Ali Khamenei, was elected Supreme Leader in a "unanimous vote".[^28] [^29] [^30]

## Geography

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Iran-geographic_map.svg/330px-Iran-geographic_map.svg.png)

The Topography of Iran

Iran has an area of 1,648,195 km <sup>2</sup> (636,372 mi <sup>2</sup>), making it is the [sixth-largest country entirely in Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Asian_countries_by_area "List of Asian countries by area") and the second-largest in West Asia.[^184] It lies between latitudes 24° and 40° N and longitudes 44° and 64° E. It is bordered to the northwest by [Armenia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenia "Armenia"), the Azeri exclave of [Nakhchivan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nakhchivan_Autonomous_Republic "Nakhchivan Autonomous Republic"),[^185] and the [Republic of Azerbaijan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azerbaijan "Azerbaijan"); to the north by the [Caspian Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caspian_Sea "Caspian Sea"); to the northeast by [Turkmenistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkmenistan "Turkmenistan"); to the east by [Afghanistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghanistan "Afghanistan") and Pakistan; to the south by the [Persian Gulf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_Gulf "Persian Gulf") and the [Gulf of Oman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_of_Oman "Gulf of Oman"); and to the west by [Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq "Iraq") and Turkey.

Iran is in a seismically active area.[^186] On average, an earthquake of [magnitude](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moment_magnitude_scale "Moment magnitude scale") 7.0 or higher occurs once every ten years.[^187] Most earthquakes are shallow-focus and can be very devastating, such as the [2003 Bam earthquake](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2003_Bam_earthquake "2003 Bam earthquake"). Iran consists mostly of the [Iranian Plateau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Plateau "Iranian Plateau"), with its southwestern region on the [Arabian plate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_plate "Arabian plate").

Iran is one of the world's most mountainous countries; its landscape is dominated by rugged mountain ranges that separate [basins](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drainage_basin "Drainage basin") or [plateaus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plateau "Plateau"). The populous western Iran is the most mountainous, with ranges such as the [Caucasus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caucasus_Mountains "Caucasus Mountains"), [Zagros](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zagros_Mountains "Zagros Mountains"), and [Alborz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alborz "Alborz"). [Mount Damavand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mount_Damavand "Mount Damavand") is the highest point, at 5,610 m (18,406 ft), which is the highest volcano in Asia. Iran's mountains have impacted its politics and economics for centuries.

Northern Iran is covered by the lush lowland [Caspian Hyrcanian forests](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyrcanian_forests "Hyrcanian forests"), near the southern shores of the Caspian Sea. The east consists mostly of [desert](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Desert "Desert") basins, such as the [Kavir Desert](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dasht-e_Kavir "Dasht-e Kavir"), which is the country's largest desert, and the [Lut Desert](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dasht-e_Loot "Dasht-e Loot"), as well as salt lakes. The Lut Desert features the highest recorded land skin temperature in the world with 70.7 °C recorded in 2005.[^188] [^189] [^190] [^191] Large plains are found along the coast of the Caspian and at the north end of the Persian Gulf, where Iran borders the mouth of the [Arvand river](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shatt_al-Arab "Shatt al-Arab"). Smaller, discontinuous plains are found along the remaining coast of the Persian Gulf, [Strait of Hormuz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strait_of_Hormuz "Strait of Hormuz"), and Gulf of Oman.[^192] [^193] [^194]

### Climate

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Koppen-Geiger_Map_IRN_present.svg/250px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_IRN_present.svg.png)

A Köppen climate classification map of Iran

Iran's climate is diverse, ranging from [arid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Desert_climate "Desert climate") and [semi-arid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semi-arid_climate "Semi-arid climate") to [subtropical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subtropics "Subtropics") along the Caspian coast and northern forests.[^195] On the north edge of Iran, temperatures rarely fall below freezing and the area remains humid. Summer temperatures rarely exceed 29 °C (84.2 °F).[^196] Annual precipitation is 680 mm (26.8 in) in the eastern plains and more than 1,700 mm (66.9 in) in the west. The UN Resident Coordinator for Iran has said that " [water scarcity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Water_scarcity "Water scarcity") poses the most severe human security challenge in Iran today." [^197]

To the west, settlements in the Zagros basin have lower temperatures and severe winters, with freezing average daily temperatures and heavy snowfall. The east and central basins are arid, with less than 200 mm (7.9 in) of rain and have occasional deserts.[^198] Average summer temperatures may reach 38 °C (100.4 °F). The southern coastal plains of the Persian Gulf and Gulf of Oman have mild winters, and very humid and hot summers. The annual precipitation ranges from 135 to 355 mm (5.3 to 14.0 in).[^199]

### Biodiversity

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Persian_Leopard_sitting.jpg/250px-Persian_Leopard_sitting.jpg)

A Persian leopard, native to the Iranian Plateau

Nearly 60% of Iran is mountainous, and less than 10% is forested.[^200] About 120 million hectares of forests and fields are government-owned for national exploitation.[^201] [^202] Iran's forests can be divided into five vegetation regions: the Hyrcanian region which forms the green belt of the north side of Iran; the [Turan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turan "Turan") region, which are mainly scattered in the center of Iran; the [Zagros region](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zagros_Mountains "Zagros Mountains"), which mainly contains oak forests in the west; the Persian Gulf region, which is scattered in the southern coastal belt; the [Arasbarani region](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arasbaran "Arasbaran"), which contains rare and unique species. More than 8,200 [plant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plant "Plant") species are grown. There are over 200 protected areas to preserve biodiversity and wildlife, with over 30 being the [national parks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_park "National park").

Iran's living fauna includes 34 bat species, [Indian grey mongoose](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_grey_mongoose "Indian grey mongoose"), [small Indian mongoose](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Small_Indian_mongoose "Small Indian mongoose"), [golden jackal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_jackal "Golden jackal"), [Indian wolf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_wolf "Indian wolf"), [foxes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fox "Fox"), [striped hyena](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Striped_hyena "Striped hyena"), [leopard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leopard "Leopard"), [Eurasian lynx](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurasian_lynx "Eurasian lynx"), [brown bear](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brown_bear "Brown bear") and [Asian black bear](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asian_black_bear "Asian black bear"). [Ungulate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ungulate "Ungulate") species include [wild boar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wild_boar "Wild boar"), [urial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urial "Urial"), [Armenian mouflon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenian_mouflon "Armenian mouflon"), [red deer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_deer "Red deer"), and [goitered gazelle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Goitered_gazelle "Goitered gazelle").[^203] [^204] The critically endangered [Asiatic cheetah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asiatic_cheetah "Asiatic cheetah") survives only in Iran. Iran lost all its [Asiatic lions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asiatic_lion "Asiatic lion") and the extinct [Caspian tigers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caspian_tiger "Caspian tiger") by the early 20th century.[^205] Domestic ungulates are represented by [sheep](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sheep "Sheep"), [goat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Goat "Goat"), [cattle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cattle "Cattle"), [horse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Horse "Horse"), [water buffalo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Water_buffalo "Water buffalo"), [donkey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donkey "Donkey") and [camel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Camel "Camel"). Iran is home to more than 570 bird species, including the [pheasant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pheasant "Pheasant"), [partridge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Partridge "Partridge"), [stork](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stork "Stork"), [eagle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eagle "Eagle"), and [falcon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Falcon "Falcon").[^206] [^207] [^208]

## Government and politics

### Supreme Leader

[^1]: Includes [Gilaks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gilaks "Gilaks") and [Mazanderanis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mazanderanis "Mazanderanis")

[^2]: Ultimate authority is vested in the [Supreme Leader](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Leader_of_Iran "Supreme Leader of Iran"), a position above the President.

[^3]: English: [/ ɪ.ˈ r ɑː n /](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/English "Help:IPA/English") [*ih-RAHN*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key "Help:Pronunciation respelling key") [Persian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_language "Persian language"): ایران, [romanized](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romanization_of_Persian "Romanization of Persian"): *Irân*, pronounced [\[ʔiːˈɾɒːn\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/Persian "Help:IPA/Persian")

[^4]: [Persian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_language "Persian language"): جمهوری اسلامی ایران, [romanized](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romanization_of_Persian "Romanization of Persian"): *Jomhuri-ye Eslâmi-ye Irân*, pronounced [\[dʒomhuːˈɾiːje eslɒːˈmiːje ʔiːˈɾɒːn\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/Persian "Help:IPA/Persian") .

[^5]: English: [/ ˈ p ɜːr ʒ ə /](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/English "Help:IPA/English") [*PUR-zhə*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key "Help:Pronunciation respelling key").;[^23] [Persian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_language "Persian language"): پارس, [romanized](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romanization_of_Persian "Romanization of Persian"): *Pârs*, pronounced [\[pʰɒːɹs\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/Persian "Help:IPA/Persian")

[^6]: The Parni was an eastern Iranian tribe established on the Amu Darya in the confederation of [Dahae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dahae "Dahae").[^66] To Yarshater, they were a [Saka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sakas "Sakas") tribe, who penetrated Parthia, adopted its language, and eventually challenged the Seleucids' power in Parthia.[^67]

[^7]: [Persian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_language "Persian language"): رهبر معظم, [romanized](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romanization_of_Persian "Romanization of Persian"): *Rahbar-e Moazam*

[^8]: "Appointing and dismissing the chief of the general staff, the commander-in-chief of the Islamic Revolution Guards Corps, and the commanders of the armed forces." [^214]

[^9]: "Declaring war and peace, and the mobilization of the armed forces." [^214]

[^10]: Officially the Ansar Allah, *de facto* government in Northwestern Yemen since 28 July 2016 under the [Supreme Political Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Political_Council "Supreme Political Council")

[^13]: "The *Factbook* puts 'Persian and Persian dialects' at 58 percent, but 51 percent of the population as ethnic Persians, while the Library of Congress states that Persian 'is spoken as a mother tongue by at least 65 percent of the population and as a second language by a large proportion of the remaining 35 percent. The 'Persian' mentioned in the latter report must thus also include Gilaki and Mazi. However, Gilaki and Mazi are actually from a different branch of the Iranian language subfamily than Persian, and could be as such be seen not as dialects, but as distinct languages. Suffice it here to say that while some scholars see categories such as Gilakis and Mazandaranis as referring to separate ethnic groups due to their linguistic traits, others count them as 'Persians' on exactly the same basis." [^577]
